Dr. Defaii has been my dentist and for all 5 of my children for 18 years. He has all the qualities of a superb dentist; clean, professional, personable, holds his staff to high standards, keeps up with the latest gadgets and innovations in dentistry.  He has lots of options for pain control for small children and gets the job done.  However, the quality that really stands out with Dr. Defaii is his extraordinary dedication to a person's teeth.  He educates the patient on how to maintain exceptionally high standards in dental hygiene.  He has a tidy, meticulous, fastidious personality and he focuses all that on your teeth!  Genetically, I was not blessed with great teeth, and Dr. Defaii seems to put himself under a little bit of stress to make them as perfect as he can.  I had a case of periodontal disease before I came to Dr. Defaii as a patient and I have not had a recurrence in 20 years.

Dr. Defaii also has absolutely the most exceptional Office Manager I have ever seen in my life to navigate all those insurance and payment headaches.  I never said anything but I always wondered, where Dr. Defaii found someone so intelligent, competent, professional, meticulous with numbers, insurance issues, personable and loyal! < review>
Awesome place I was from out of state and had a tire blow out not only did they have it in stock they got right to fixing my tire.</review>
<pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO8XCf8ys9qqVnDLJL2dLehKYDBSHQEFQDjcrwc=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pictures><Response>None<//Response>< GmapID>

<Rate>5<//Rate><Resp>None< /Resp><Pictures>None</Pictures>< text>
From what I've read, tire plugs typically cost $5 or less, so the fact Snyder's charges $10 isn't great, but things tend to be more expensive in the mountains and I'm still happy with their service.  They were overloaded and missing two mechanics today before a storm is due, but one of their mechanics was still willing to take the time to talk to me on the phone about fixing a screw in my tire.  He recommended the cheaper plug over a patch from the inside because plugs tend to last longer in our weather.  Plugs are quick to install so he had the first one done in a few minutes.  While I waited, I noticed another tire also had a screw in it!  I rolled my car and the mechanic checked each tire and we found a third tire had a much older beat up screw in it.  All the screws were only half an inch so I'm not sure any were actually causing leaks yet, although I'd noticed the pressure on two of the tires was abnormally low a week ago.  He charged me $20 instead of $30 for all three and it was done in about 10 minutes.  He also filled every tire with air to 40psi which he said is recommended on our curvy roads.

Also, I often find tire places will try to upsell you on things like getting an alignment or replacing your tires because the treads are worn but there were none of those shenanigans here.

UPDATE: I came back two years later to ask if I should worry about a cut in the sidewall of a tire about 1" long and 1/4" deep.  They inspected it and said nothing to worry about.  I'm pleased they didn't try to sell me repairs I didn't need.< /text>

California Department of Consumer Affairs - Medical Board

< Review>
I gave birth here in Feb. 2021. The experience was awful.

They ran out of epidural when I was 9cm dilated and I was forced to wait over 90 minutes for the anesthesiologist to return from a different surgery to medicate me. I was told, ‚Äúwell, it‚Äôs Saturday.‚Äù

The c-section nurses were unprofessional and while I was panicking (sobbing/hyperventilating), they giggled and talked loudly about other things while they readied my body for the unexpected surgery. Then they forced a catheter inside of me without medication. I screamed ‚Äúplease stop!‚Äù over and over. They held me down and forced it in. No one explained to me why they needed to do this. It still haunts me. I‚Äôve never lost my agency like that. It traumatized me.

In postpartum care, the nurses were unprofessional, irritable, and forgetful. The bathroom did not have a shower head, so I was told to use a hand wash cloth to bathe myself at the sink daily. This was after days of laboring. The nurses used my water bottle (for my privates) to clean the toilet when I used it. The bathroom floor was always wet and filthy. The second time I used the toilet, the nurse helped me get there, then said she had to see to something and would send someone to help me off. No one ever came.

The nurses told me that my breasts were ‚Äúbad‚Äù for breastfeeding and insisted that I allow them to feed my daughter formula. I refused. One got so irritated, she watched me struggle to breastfeed, and when my daughter started crying, she said ‚ÄúSee! She‚Äôs hungry!‚Äù Then she stormed out of the room. It was awful behavior. (My daughter has been successfully exclusively breastfed). The PP nurses were just awful.

I left after only 2 days in recovery (typical time for c-section is 4 days). The food was horrendous. The PP nurses were atrocious to me. The surgery was traumatizing. There are other hospitals on the west side to have your baby‚Äîdon‚Äôt choose this one.</Review>

< Review>
My nose surgery was at St John's Ambulatory Surgery Center. Meghan the nurse who prepped me as I went in for surgery was very kind. She explained everything that she was doing and took much care to make sure that I was as comfortable as possible every step of the way. She also called me the day before the surgery with preparation instructions.

The surgery took 1.5 hours. Both Dr Kieu and my nurse each called my wife to tell her how the surgery went (smoothly) and when she could pick me up. Timeline for the day:
- arrived at 5:30
- surgery at 7
- recovery room at 8:45
- left at 10

I had three nose surgeries done all at once:
- septoplasty
- bilateral inferior turbinate reduction
- repair of nasal vestibular stenosis (bilateral) (using latera implants)

Excluding the cost for the surgeon, $12,432.66 was billed to my insurer (includes anesthesiologist, facility, drugs they pump into me before, during, and after surgery, etc). I paid much less than that, but that is what was billed to my insurer.

They tried to get me to pre-pay a massive amount to cover the maximum estimated cost I was expected to have to pay for the surgery, which I pushed back against since the fact that I was getting three surgeries done at once meant that I would likely get them at a discount since they shared 'overhead'. The person on the phone quickly gave in and said 'then what amount are you comfortable prepaying'? I told him '$400' and he was fine with that.

Here are the rev code translations for reference:
0250: pharmacy
0636: pharmacy
0370: anesthesia
0272: medical/surgical supplies
0278: surgical supplies/implant
0360: operating room
0710: recovery room<//Review>

I spent 5 hours in the ER d/t extreme abdominal pain. While the doctor and registration staff was pleasant, the hospital nursing staff was inexcusably unprofessional, uncaring, and down-right dangerous. The first nurse put an IV and pressed on my vein constantly d/t slow blood flow. Then I noticed my arm was stinging and swelling up with fluid. She sent a phlebotomist in and he said he would go get her. NEITHER of them ever came back. My mom had to search for a nurse 45 minutes later and she stared at my swollen arm and said, "the last nurse didn't give you fluid so you shouldn't be bubbling. You should be fine." I proceeded to politely ask for her to take it out and asked if I would have my blood test completed....she replied, "oh, the doctor said you didn't need it." I had come in for pain and it literally took 3 hours to get my pain meds. I had to beg for some relief....later, (I won't give the gory details) I was trying to clean myself and asked for a nurse's help. As I was cleaning myself I got really dizzy and nauseous and almost fell. I was not wearing any bottoms and the nurse instructed me to walk to the restroom. I told her I couldn't walk and needed to sit and possibly throw up. She continued to instruct me to walk to the restroom. Btw, I came in a wheelchair because I couldn't walk.....After a few minutes of going back and forth with her, I asked her just to put a large pad on the bed so I could sit and asked for nausea medication. She came back 30 minutes later with a Rx and said she couldn't give me the medication because they had already discharged me....I am a typically positive person and I was polite to everyone involved, but if I can save someone the pain of going to their ER, then I believe it's worth posting.<//review>

< review>
Magicland is just that, with play areas, a theater, TVs showing kid movies at each dental chair and a drawer of toys for kids to choose from, it is a welcoming environment for young children. The dentists and staff are friendly, helpful and do a great job of putting the kids at ease. My son had to have teeth extracted and that process was as gentle as possible. The only reason I gave 4 stars instead of 5 is because I would have liked more information on the post-extraction care. For example, how long should he only eat soft/liquid food? Does he brush his teeth and mouthwash as usual same day? I was too distracted to ask these questions at the time, now I have to Google for answers.< /review>

< review>
It's been about 6 years since by son has been here but I saw some of the reviews for this place and wanted to share what happened when I took my then 5 year old there which I believed has caused him long term psychological fear of dentistry

He had a few cavities to get fixed.  They gave him a couple of pills to  relax him before the procedure, which didn't work at all. So they tied him up in a papoose then took him into a private room, stuck an instrument to keep his mouth open so they could work on him.  I could hear him SCREAMING in TERROR and horror the whole time.  I asked if I could go in to calm him down but they wouldn't allow me saying it's some privacy issue.  They had absolutely NO REACTION OR COMPASSION. My child was a cattle being herded through for them to get their insurance money.

Looking back at it now and seeing the results it has had on my son I consider it CHILD ABUSE what they did.   The front office looks beautiful and gives the illusion that it is so kid friendly BUT IT'S ALL SMOKE AND MIRROR.

Thank God I found an amazing and gentle dentist after this incident, Dr. David Suh (in Lomita).  I told him about this incident and he was flabbergasted.  My son to this day still has a hard time having Dr. Suh work on him but it's gotten so much better because Dr. Suh will let me sit in the room and hold his hand to reassure him the whole time. (No such thing as "Privacy Issue" like at Magic Land).  And when he gets too scared Dr. Suh will stop, joke with him or walk out to give me so some time to help him calm down.  He never tries to rush us to get the next person in.

I certainly hope this place has changed their practice by now.  If your child has simple quick and easy work to be done or has no anxiety or fear then go to this place.   But I still would recommend STAYING CLEAR FROM THIS PLACE and encourage you to find a small private family dental office that is focused on the patients well being and not their bottom line.<//review>

< Review>
No Magic beyond the doorstep.
I don't normally right reviews unless I am so impressed or so upset with the experience. This is by far, the worst and most traumatizing experience you can put you kid into. You, like me, will be fooled by the colors of the place, the little movie theater (you barely can see the picture), or the toys and drawings on the walls. From the moment you are waiting to be checked in, you will realize that you didn't expect you, they barely have time for you, they have no order, they have no line, it is first jump first served, and you will be lucky if they will actually serve you and not tell you "I'll be with you in a second" and then they don't.
We were initially referred here because our 5 years old has a cavity that needed filing and our regular dentist didn't have laughing gas, so we came here to have them give her laughing gas.
WARNING: Insurance doesn't cover laughing gas, so they will charge you $150 for laughing gas only. And if instead you choose the other option "the drink that makes your baby "Drunk" so that he/she forgets the horrifying experience" then the bill is even higher for this little cup ($220).
